type="application/ld+json">{"@context":"http://schema.org","@type":"NewsArticle","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://www.orlandosentinel.com/coronavirus/os-ne-florida-coronavirus-wednesday-october-7-20201007-s5h54oaafne3rliynudw6vcxcq-story.html"},"headline":"Florida Florida resident death toll from coronavirus rose to 14,904 with an additional 137 fatalities reported by the state Department of Health on Wednesday.With 180 non-Florida resident deaths, the combined death toll stands at 15,084.The state also reported an additional 2,582 positive COVID-19 infection results, now having logged 722,707 cases to date.Based on the state\xe2\x80\x99s nearly 21.5 million population, about one in every 1,440 people in the state have died from the virus. The state\xe2\x80\x99s fatality reporting includes deaths from several previous days, as it can take two weeks or more for them to be logged.Infections have steadied in the last month, hovering in the 2,000-3,000 range daily most days.The Florida Department of Health hasn\xe2\x80\x99t reported a daily increase above 10,000 infections since July 25. But testing has declined statewide, to a daily average of about 22,700 since September 1. That\xe2\x80\x99s down from about 32,000 daily tests on average in August and 54,400 a day in July.Over 5.4 million people have been tested in Florida, with 26,128 more tests reported Wednesday compared with the previous day.Statewide, the latest positivity rate reported by the Florida Department of Health was 4.15%, but that\xe2\x80\x99s for new cases only and excludes anyone who previously tested positive. For all cases including retests of those previously infected, the latest positivity rate is 5.33%. (Read more: Florida\xe2\x80\x99s hidden data skews COVID-19 test results)Central Florida on Wednesday added 532 cases for a total of 115,372: 191 new cases in Orange for 41,409; 100 in Polk for 20,687; 53 in Osceola for 12,899; 45 in Volusia for 11,235; 57 in Brevard for 9,568; 31 in Seminole for 9,309; 41 in Lake for 7,770; and 14 in Sumter for 2,495. (See details on all Central Florida cases here).Central Florida had 30 of Wednesday\xe2\x80\x99s newly reported deaths, bringing the region\xe2\x80\x99s toll to 2,284. That includes 10 new deaths in Polk, six in Volusia, four each in Orange and Osceola, three in Lake, two in Brevard and one in Seminole County. No new deaths were reported in Sumter County.Polk County, due to nursing-home outbreaks, has the most coronavirus fatalities in the region with 542, followed by 491 in Orange, 311 in Brevard, 271 in Volusia, 229 in Seminole, 199 in Lake, 168 in Osceola, and 73 in Sumter.Central Florida accounts for nearly 16% of the cases statewide and 15% of the deaths.COVID-19 hospitalizations have been steadily falling from mid-July highs of over 8,000. Across the state, 2,132 people were hospitalized with COVID-19 as of about 10:30 a.m. Wednesday. The state\xe2\x80\x99s online tool updates several times throughout the day.Orange County reported 146 patients hospitalized, Osceola with 71, Seminole with 24, and Lake with 40 as of about 10:30 a.m. Wednesday.To date, 45,259 people have been hospitalized in Florida, the state\xe2\x80\x99s COVID-19 dashboard shows. But those numbers could include cases that are weeks old.South Florida, home to 29% of Florida\xe2\x80\x99s population, accounts for about 41% of cases with 299,038 total. That includes 809 new cases reported Wednesday among Miami-Dade, Broward, and Palm Beach counties.South Florida\xe2\x80\x99s reported deaths rose by 42 on Wednesday for a total of 6,216, about 42% of the state\xe2\x80\x99s total.The latest breakdown of Florida\xe2\x80\x99s coronavirus cases can be found here, and county-by-county data can be found here.List of mobile coronavirus and antibody testing sites in Central Florida by countyThe virus has infected nearly 36 million people and has killed over 1 million worldwide, according to the Johns Hopkins University &amp;amp; Medicine Coronavirus Resource Center. Nationwide, over 7.5 million people have been infected and nearly 211,000 are dead.As the summer coronavirus spike in Sunbelt states subsides, Florida has gone the furthest in lifting restrictions, especially on restaurants where the burden of ensuring safety has shifted to business owners and residents \xe2\x80\x94 raising concerns of a resurgence.Though Gov. Ron DeSantis generally wears a mask when arriving at public appearances and has allowed municipalities to impose mask rules, he has declined to impose a statewide mandate. And on Sept. 25, as the state entered a Phase 3 reopening, he barred municipalities from collecting fines for mask violations.Since April, America has led the world by far in sheer numbers of confirmed infections and deaths. The U.S. has less than 5% of the globe\xe2\x80\x99s population but more than 20% of the reported deaths.Black and Hispanic people and American Indians have accounted for a disproportionate share of the deaths, underscoring the economic and health care disparities in the U.S.Millions of Americans are counting on a COVID-19 vaccine to curb the pandemic and return life to normal. While one or more options could be available toward the end of this year or early next, the path to delivering vaccines to 330 million people remains unclear for the local health officials expected to carry out the work.Many Americans have resisted wearing masks and social distancing, calling such precautions an overreaction or an infringement on their liberty. Public health experts say the problem has been compounded by confusing and inconsistent guidance from politicians and a patchwork quilt of approaches to containing the scourge by county, state and federal governments.Brazil has the second-most fatalities with over 147,000, India with over 104,000, Mexico with over 82,000, the United Kingdom with over 42,000, Italy with over 36,000, and Peru, France and Spain with over 32,000.In the U.S., New York\xe2\x80\x99s deadly outbreak in the spring accounted for most of the deaths with more than 33,000, followed by Texas, California and New Jersey with more than 16,000 each.Florida is fifth in the nation in overall deaths, but based on population, ranks 11th per capita, according to numbers on Statista.com.In terms of fatalities compared to overall population, Florida is seeing a 0.07% death rate. In terms of deaths compared to those infected, it\xe2\x80\x99s seeing a 2% death rate, meaning about one in 48 people who are infected with it die. That number is one in 36 nationally and one in 34 globally, but in reality, the actual number of cases around the world is believed to be much higher than reported \xe2\x80\x94 perhaps 10 times higher in the U.S., according to the CDC \xe2\x80\x94 given testing limitations and the many mild cases that have gone unreported or unrecognized. So death rates would be lower since cases have gone unreported.Some of the worst-hit nations have been those whose leaders have downplayed the severity of COVID-19, undercut the advice of health experts and pushed unproven remedies.Have a comment about this story? Share it on our Facebook page.You can sign up for new daily Florida coronavirus update by subscribing to The Health Report newsletter and as-they-happen Breaking News emails at OrlandoSentinel.com/newsletters.Join our Facebook group \xe2\x80\x9cCoronavirus news from the Orlando Sentinel\xe2\x80\x9dJuan Carlos Sosa has been described as \xe2\x80\x9cJuan in a million,\xe2\x80\x9d but for his family he is \xe2\x80\x9cJuan the one and only.\xe2\x80\x9d Whenever someone needed help, there he was, willing to assist, no matter the day or time. Now, he will no longer greet students with a big smile when they arrive at Celebration K-8 school and will never be able sing in the car with his daughter. Juan Carlos died on Aug. 30 at age 57. His family believes he was infected with coronavirus after he celebrated his birthday at the school where he was a custodian.Deborah Denise Henson spent much of her adult life in pain \xe2\x80\x94 the result of a freakish accident that left her with plates and screws in her back. But you wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have known it from her smile. She survived a host of medical problems before succumbing to COVID-19.Pong Hui Chartier, known as \xe2\x80\x9cConnie\xe2\x80\x9d to customers at the dry cleaning business she operated in Ocoee, liked to do things her way. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s never been someone that rested. She was always go, go, go. If anyone was going to live to be 100, it would be my mother,\xe2\x80\x9d her daughter said. At 79, Pong Hui took only one medication \xe2\x80\x94 for her thyroid. But in early March, she was diagnosed with pneumonia. Weeks later, she died as a victim of coronavirus.See more Central Florida coronavirus obituaries here.Are you feeling stressed or depressed from the COVID19 outbreak? There are resources available for you. You can contact the Disaster Distress Helpline at 1-800-985-5990 or visit https://www.samhsa.gov/disaster-preparednessAvoid close contact with people who are sick.Stay home when you are sick and avoid contact with people in poor health.Don\xe2\x80\x99t touch your eyes, nose and mouth with unwashed hands.Cover your cough or sneeze with a tissue, then dispose of the tissue.Wash your hands often with soap and water for at least 20 seconds, especially after going to the bathroom, before eating, and after blowing your nose, coughing or sneezing.Clean and disinfect touched objects and surfaces using a regular household cleaning spray or wipe.Follow these recommendations for using a face mask: The CDC now recommends wearing cloth face coverings in public settings where other social-distancing measures are difficult to maintain (e.g., grocery stores and pharmacies), especially in areas of significant community-based transmission. Follow these guidelines for using a cloth mask.The Florida Department of Health has set up a call center to answer questions about coronavirus. There\xe2\x80\x99s a number for Orange County, too.The Florida Department of Health\xe2\x80\x99s number is 1-866-779-6121 and is available Tuesday through Friday, 8 a.m. to 7 p.m. Residents may also email questions to COVID-19@flhealth.gov.In Orange County, the number to call is 407-723-5004; it\xe2\x80\x99s available Tuesday through Friday, 8 a.m. to 5 p.m.For mental-health help, here is a list of resources.The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention: cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncovThe Florida Department of Health: floridahealth.gov/diseases-and-conditions/COVID-19. But testing has declined statewide, to a daily average of about 22,700 since September 1. That\xe2\x80\x99s down from about 32,000 daily tests on average in August and 54,400 a day in July.</p> </div></div> <div data-type="text" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <p class=""> Over 5.4 million people have been tested in Florida, with 26,128 more tests reported Wednesday compared with the previous day.</p> </div></div> <div class="mobile-nativo inline-ad hddn-dktp" data-inline-ad-count="3"> <div class="wrapper clearfix pb-curated full pb-feature pb-layout-item pb-f-ads-nativo" data-pb-name="Nativo Ad" data-pb-curated="curated" data-pb-id="unnamed-feature" id="feT0AZ1q1Kxwds"> <div id="3068" class="trb_ar_nt_m"> </div> </div></div> <div data-type="raw_html" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <div class="element element-rawhtml "> <iframe title="Florida COVID-19 cases by date" aria-label="Interactive line chart" id="datawrapper-chart-jKg0n" src="https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/jKg0n/68/" scrolling="no" frameborder="0" style="width: 0px; border: none; height: 400px; min-width: 100% !important;" height="400"></iframe></div></div></div> <div data-type="text" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <p class=""> Statewide, the latest positivity rate reported by the Florida Department of Health was 4.15%, but that\xe2\x80\x99s for new cases only and excludes anyone who previously tested positive. Now, he will no longer greet students with a big smile when they arrive at Celebration K-8 school and will never be able sing in the car with his daughter. Juan Carlos died on Aug. 30 at age 57. His family believes he was infected with coronavirus after he celebrated his birthday at the school where he was a custodian.</li> <li> <a href="https://www.orlandosentinel.com/coronavirus/obituaries/os-ne-coronavirus-obit-deborah-denise-henson-20200715-p4rasy73lnb3pdypqzff2pfxge-story.html" target="_blank">Deborah Denise Henson spent much of her adult life in pain</a> \xe2\x80\x94 the result of a freakish accident that left her with plates and screws in her back. But you wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have known it from her smile. She survived a host of medical problems before succumbing to COVID-19.</li> <li> <a href="https://www.orlandosentinel.com/coronavirus/obituaries/os-ne-coronavirus-obit-pong-hui-chartier-winter-garden-20200702-5ee32kaicjcuvnwudowb75oxbe-story.html" target="_blank">Pong Hui Chartier, known as \xe2\x80\x9cConnie\xe2\x80\x9d to customers</a> at the dry cleaning business she operated in Ocoee, liked to do things her way. \xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s never been someone that rested. She was always go, go, go. If anyone was going to live to be 100, it would be my mother,\xe2\x80\x9d her daughter said. At 79, Pong Hui took only one medication \xe2\x80\x94 for her thyroid. But in early March, she was diagnosed with pneumonia. Weeks later, she died as a victim of coronavirus.</li> </ul> </div> </div></div> <div data-type="story" class="crd crd-pll-lf "> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <div class=" align-items-start Do this</h2></div></div> <div data-type="text" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <p class=""> Are you feeling stressed or depressed from the COVID19 outbreak? There are resources available for you. You can contact the Disaster Distress Helpline at 1-800-985-5990 or visit <a href="https://www.samhsa.gov/disaster-preparedness">https://www.samhsa.gov/disaster-preparedness</a></p> </div></div> <div data-type="header" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <h2 class="h5 heavy-text"> How to protect yourself</h2></div></div> <div data-type="list" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <div class=""> <ul class="element-ul"> <li> Avoid close contact with people who are sick.</li> <li> Stay home when you are sick and avoid contact with people in poor health.</li> <li> Don\xe2\x80\x99t touch your eyes, nose and mouth with unwashed hands.</li> <li> Cover your cough or sneeze with a tissue, then dispose of the tissue.</li> <li> Wash your hands often with soap and water for at least 20 seconds, especially after going to the bathroom, before eating, and after blowing your nose, coughing or sneezing.</li> <li> Clean and disinfect touched objects and surfaces using a regular household cleaning spray or wipe.</li> </ul> </div> </div></div> <div data-type="text" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <p class=""> Follow these recommendations for using a face mask: The <a href="https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/prevent-getting-sick/cloth-face-cover.html">CDC now recommends</a> wearing cloth face coverings in public settings where other social-distancing measures are difficult to maintain (e.g., grocery stores and pharmacies), especially in areas of significant community-based transmission. <a href="https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/prevent-getting-sick/diy-cloth-face-coverings.html" target="_blank"><b>Follow these guidelines for using a cloth mask.</b></a></p> </div></div> <div data-type="header" class="crd clln--it"> <div class=" crd--cnt "> <h2 class="h5 heavy-text"> Questions?
